        <span>In addition to a high specific capacity and low OCVs, a high charging or discharging rate capability is essential for a promising anode material. The rate performance of anode materials is affected by the ionic diffusion coefficient related to the diffusion energy barrier. In <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5</a>, it is obvious that the adsorption energy difference between S1 and S2 is smaller than that between S2 and S3 for the same system. Hence, Li/Na ions prefer diffusing along the S1S2S1 path on the surfaces of Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> as shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig11">Fig. 11a and b</a>, respectively. We calculated the Li/Na diffusion energy barriers of Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> by the CI-NEB method. As shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig11">Fig. 11c and d</a>, for the Li<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>/Na<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>M<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> configurations at delithiated/desodiated states, the Li/Na diffusion energy barriers of Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> are 27/14 and 16/12 meV, respectively, which are significantly lower than those of graphene,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit18"><sup><span class="sup_ref">18</span></sup></a> MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small><a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit25"><sup><span class="sup_ref">25</span></sup></a> and MXenes.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit13"><sup><span class="sup_ref">13,28,54</span></sup></a> Besides, it is easier for Na ions to diffuse than Li ions owning to their lower diffusion energy barriers. Furthermore, we calculated the diffusion coefficients of Li/Na atom on the Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayers according to <a title="" href="#eqn8">eqn (8)</a>. The results are listed in Table S8.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> The diffusion coefficients of Li/Na on Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> at 300 K are 2.6  10<small><sup>3</sup></small>/4.3  10<small><sup>3</sup></small> and 3.7  10<small><sup>3</sup></small>/4.3  10<small><sup>3</sup></small> cm<small><sup>2</sup></small> s<small><sup>1</sup></small>, respectively, which are significantly higher than graphene (6.0  10<small><sup>7</sup></small> cm<small><sup>2</sup></small> s<small><sup>1</sup></small> for Li)<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit18"><sup><span class="sup_ref">18</span></sup></a> and most hexagonal transition metal MBene.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit34"><sup><span class="sup_ref">34</span></sup></a> For the Li<small><sub>2</sub></small>/Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>M<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> configurations at fully lithiated/sodiated states, the Li/Na ions on different surface of the monolayers migrate in an alternating way by one side stationary and the other side moving as a whole with the lowest diffusion energy barriers. In <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig11">Fig. 11e and f</a>, the corresponding Li/Na diffusion energy barriers of Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> at are 187/58 and 52/34 meV, respectively. It is worth noting that the Li diffusion energy barrier of Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> at the 6<small><sup>th</sup></small> site is 56 meV arising from the alternative migration ions on different side of the Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayer. The diffusion energy barriers for the fully lithiated/sodiated states of Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> is higher than that of the delithiated/desodiated states because the repulsive interactions between Li/Na ions on the surface of the monolayers. However, the energy barriers for full lithiation/sodiation is still much lower than that for delithiation/desodiation in graphite (4501200 meV),<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit10"><sup><span class="sup_ref">10</span></sup></a> indicating that Li/Na ions possess strong migration ability on the surface of Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small>.</span>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig11"><a href="/image/article/2024/NR/d4nr01786b/d4nr01786b-f11_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d4nr01786b-f11.tif" src="/image/article/2024/NR/d4nr01786b/d4nr01786b-f11.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 11 </b> <span id="fig11"><span class="graphic_title">Li/Na migration paths on (a) Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and (b) Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayers, along with the corresponding Li/Na diffusion energy barriers for (c) Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and (d) Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> delithiated/desodiated states, as well as the Li/Na diffusion energy barriers for (e) Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and (f) Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> at lithiated/sodiated states. The Li<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>/Na<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>M<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Li<small><sub>2</sub></small>/Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>M<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> configurations are investigated for delithiated/desodiated and lithiated/sodiated states, respectively.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      
      
        
        <h3 id="sect1530"><span class="b_heading">3.8 Comparison with other anode materials</span></h3>
        <span>To evaluate the performance of Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayers as anode materials for LIBs and NIBs, we compared their theoretical specific capacities and average voltages with MBenes, MXenes and other 2D materials as shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig12">Fig. 12</a>. In the plot of average voltage <span class="italic">vs.</span> theoretical capacity, the closer the data point is to the lower right corner, the better the overall performance of the anode material with higher theoretical specific capacity and lower average voltage. In <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig12">Fig. 12a</a>, the theoretical specific capacity of the Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayer for LIBs (764 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>) surpasses that of the WB<small><sub>4</sub></small> (708 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>),<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit55"><sup><span class="sup_ref">55</span></sup></a> SbP<small><sub>3</sub></small> (499 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>),<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit58"><sup><span class="sup_ref">58</span></sup></a> and VSeTe (416 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>)<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit59"><sup><span class="sup_ref">59</span></sup></a> monolayers, the orthorhombic Fe<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> (665 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>) and Mo<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> (444 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>) MBenes,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit30"><sup><span class="sup_ref">30</span></sup></a> as well as the hexagonal Zr<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> (764 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>),<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit36"><sup><span class="sup_ref">36</span></sup></a> Sc<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> (480 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>)<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit34"><sup><span class="sup_ref">34</span></sup></a> and Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> (456 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>)<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit35"><sup><span class="sup_ref">35</span></sup></a> MBenes and the Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small> (448 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>)<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit28"><sup><span class="sup_ref">28</span></sup></a> MXene. Moreover, the diffusion energy barriers of Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayer for Li atoms (27 meV) is much lower than graphite (4501200 meV)<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit10"><sup><span class="sup_ref">10</span></sup></a> and the orthorhombic Fe<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> (240 meV) and Mo<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> (270 meV) MBenes,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit30"><sup><span class="sup_ref">30</span></sup></a> as listed in Table S9.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> The results indicate that the Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayer is a promising anode material with excellent overall performance. The Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayer exhibits a relatively low average voltage for LIBs (0.275 V), slightly higher than that of the hexagonal Zr<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> (0.236 V).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit36"><sup><span class="sup_ref">36</span></sup></a> Additionally, its theoretical capacity for LIBs (527 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>) comparable to Zr<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> (526 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>)<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit36"><sup><span class="sup_ref">36</span></sup></a> makes Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> also a good 2D anode material. For SIBs, the theoretical specific capacity of Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> (859 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>) and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> (527 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>) monolayers are comparable to BCN (647 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>)<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit60"><sup><span class="sup_ref">60</span></sup></a> and higher than MoC<small><sub>2</sub></small> (447 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>),<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit61"><sup><span class="sup_ref">61</span></sup></a> Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>C<small><sub>2</sub></small> (352 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>),<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit28"><sup><span class="sup_ref">28</span></sup></a> Nb<small><sub>2</sub></small>Se<small><sub>2</sub></small>C (335 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>),<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit56"><sup><span class="sup_ref">56</span></sup></a> WB<small><sub>4</sub></small> (472 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>),<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit55"><sup><span class="sup_ref">55</span></sup></a> Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> (342 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>)<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit35"><sup><span class="sup_ref">35</span></sup></a> and MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small> (146 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>)<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit25"><sup><span class="sup_ref">25</span></sup></a> as shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig12">Fig. 12b</a>. Furthermore, the quite low average voltages (0.279 and 0.362 V) and diffusion energy barriers (14 and 12 meV) for Na atoms of Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayers add merits to themselves as anode materials in SIBs as show in Table S10.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a></span>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig12"><a href="/image/article/2024/NR/d4nr01786b/d4nr01786b-f12_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d4nr01786b-f12.tif" src="/image/article/2024/NR/d4nr01786b/d4nr01786b-f12.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 12 </b> <span id="fig12"><span class="graphic_title">The comparison of the theoretical capacities and the average voltages for anode materials in (a) LIBs and (b) SIBs, including MBenes, MXenes and other 2D materials.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      
      
        
        <h3 id="sect1635"><span class="b_heading">3.9 Anode performance of multilayers</span></h3>
        <span>To understand the effect of the multi-layer structures on the anode performance, we investigated the <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>ave</sub></small>, specific capacities and OCVs of M<small><sub>3</sub></small>B<small><sub>4</sub></small> and M<small><sub>4</sub></small>B<small><sub>6</sub></small> (M = Mg, Ca) for Li/Na ions. The <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>ave</sub></small> of Li<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>/Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>M<small><sub>3</sub></small>B<small><sub>4</sub></small> are displayed in Fig. S17<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> and the energy differences of <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>ave</sub></small> between the Li<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>/Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>M<small><sub>3</sub></small>B<small><sub>4</sub></small> and Li<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>/Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>M<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> configurations are listed in Table S11.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> Compared to the Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayer, there is no significant change in the <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>ave</sub></small> of the Ca<small><sub>3</sub></small>B<small><sub>4</sub></small> multilayer for Li/Na ions. The same case is observed for the <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>ave</sub></small> of the Mg<small><sub>3</sub></small>B<small><sub>4</sub></small> multilayer for Li ions. However, the <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>ave</sub></small> of the Mg<small><sub>3</sub></small>B<small><sub>4</sub></small> multilayer for Na ions decreases significantly when <span class="italic">x</span> &gt; 2, leading to an increase in the maximum Na ion concentration (<span class="italic">x</span> = 2.75). The <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>ave</sub></small> of Li<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>/Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>M<small><sub>4</sub></small>B<small><sub>6</sub></small> are displayed in Fig. S18<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> and the energy differences of <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>ave</sub></small> between the Li<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>/Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>M<small><sub>4</sub></small>B<small><sub>6</sub></small> and Li<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>/Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>M<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> configurations are listed in Table S12.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> Specifically, the <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>ave</sub></small> of the Mg<small><sub>4</sub></small>B<small><sub>6</sub></small> multilayer for Na ions also exhibits a significant decrease comparing to the Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayer, which results in the maximum Na ion concentration reaching <span class="italic">x</span> = 2.75. In this way, the calculated specific capacities of Mg<small><sub>3</sub></small>B<small><sub>4</sub></small>, Ca<small><sub>3</sub></small>B<small><sub>4</sub></small>, Mg<small><sub>4</sub></small>B<small><sub>6</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>4</sub></small>B<small><sub>6</sub></small> for Li/Na ions are 462/635, 328/328, 331/455 and 239/268 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, respectively. As the layer thickness and the molecular weight increase, the specific capacities of these MBenes exhibit varying degrees of decline, even if the number of ions adsorbed on the surface increases for some MBenes. Besides, as exhibited in Fig. S19S22,<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> the average OCVs of Mg<small><sub>3</sub></small>B<small><sub>4</sub></small>, Ca<small><sub>3</sub></small>B<small><sub>4</sub></small>, Mg<small><sub>4</sub></small>B<small><sub>6</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>4</sub></small>B<small><sub>6</sub></small> for Li/Na ions are 0.360/0.353, 0.343/0.353, 0.423/0.341 and 0.341/0.312 V, respectively, showing no significant changes compared to their corresponding monolayers. Additionally, as shown in Fig. S23,<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> the diffusion energy of Mg<small><sub>3</sub></small>B<small><sub>4</sub></small>, Ca<small><sub>3</sub></small>B<small><sub>4</sub></small>, Mg<small><sub>4</sub></small>B<small><sub>6</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>4</sub></small>B<small><sub>6</sub></small> for Li/Na ions are 22/12, 7/3, 23/12 and 29/4 meV, respectively. Among them, due to a relatively large decrease (0.070 eV) in adsorption energy from Li<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> to Li<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ca<small><sub>4</sub></small>B<small><sub>6</sub></small>, the diffusion energy of the Ca<small><sub>4</sub></small>B<small><sub>6</sub></small> multilayer for Li ions (29 meV) has increased compared to that of the Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayer (16 meV). Overall, the OCVs and Li/Na ion diffusion energy barriers of hexagonal 2D Mg and Ca borides are less affected by the multilayer structure, while the decreases in specific capacities lead to a decline in overall anode performance.</span>
      
      
        
        <h3 id="sect1755"><span class="b_heading">3.10 Effects of functionalization</span></h3>
        <span>During the synthetic process, MXenes tend to be terminated by surface functional groups, such as O, OH, and F. However, no functional groups were observed on the surfaces of synthetic Cr<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small>,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit62"><sup><span class="sup_ref">62</span></sup></a> Mo<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small>,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit63"><sup><span class="sup_ref">63</span></sup></a> and Ti<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small><a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit64"><sup><span class="sup_ref">64</span></sup></a> MBenes. Besides, using ultrasonication in suitable solvents, the unmodified 2D metal borides nanosheets were exfoliated from the bulk MB<small><sub>2</sub></small> (M = Ti, Zr, Hf, Nb, Ta, Cr, Al, and Mg).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit38"><sup><span class="sup_ref">38</span></sup></a> To investigate the O-functionalization effect on Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayers, we constructed and relaxed the Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> structures and conducted phonon calculations and AIMD simulations at 300K for 10 ps. The results are displayed in Fig. S24 in the ESI.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> The phonon spectra of Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>2</sub></small> show imaginary frequencies in the Brillouin zones indicating that the O-modified Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayers are dynamically unstable. The total energies drop fast in the first 300 steps in AIMD simulations and then maintain a certain average. The snapshots show that the inner boron atom layer produces distortion and segregation under the influence of the surface oxygen atoms. However, the entire monolayers remain in one piece. We conclude that functionalization will oxidize the structure of Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayers and affect the anode performance. Hence, the synthesis of corresponding anode materials should avoid the contamination of functionalization groups by employing strict synthetic procedures in suitable solvents.</span>
      
    
    
      
      <h2 id="sect1795"><span class="a_heading">4. Conclusion</span></h2>
      <span>In this work, we predicted two IIA metal MBenes, including Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small>, by <span class="italic">ab initio</span> calculations. The MBene family was expanded to non-transition metal borides at the first time. The robust dynamic, mechanical, and thermal stabilities of the Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayers were confirmed by phonon calculations, mechanical calculations and AIMD simulations, respectively. The band structures and DOS exhibit that Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayers possess excellent electronic conductivities conducive to their applications in ion energy storage. Benefitting from their low molecular weights and moderate adsorption for Li/Na atoms, the Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> monolayers demonstrate the superior theoretical specific capacities as 764/527 and 859/527 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> for Li/Na ions, respectively. Moreover, their robust electronical conductivities and small <span class="italic">S</span><small><sub>cross</sub></small> change ratios meet the electrical and structural requirements during charging and discharging processes. Additionally, the low OCVs attributed to the small energy differences between stable adsorption configurations and the high ion diffusion coefficients resulting from the low diffusion energy barriers further enhance the potential of Mg<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> and Ca<small><sub>2</sub></small>B<small><sub>2</sub></small> as anode materials in LIBs and SIBs. The multilayer structures have less effect on the OCVs and Li/Na ion diffusion energy barriers, while the decrease in specific capacities lead to a decline in overall anode performance. Besides, the functionalization of O groups strongly reduces the stability of the monolayers, which should be avoided in experiments. In conclusion, we predicted two new 2D hexagonal IIA metal MBenes promising for anode materials in LIBs and SIBs. Our research paves a new way to the application of the main group metal MBenes in ion energy storage.</span>

They are usually only set in response to actions made by you which amount to a request for services, such as setting your privacy preferences, logging in or filling in forms. You can set your browser to block or alert you about these cookies, but some parts of the site will not then work. These cookies do not store any personally identifiable information.</p></div></div><div class="ot-accordion-layout ot-cat-item ot-vs-config" data-optanongroupid="C0002"><button aria-expanded="false" ot-accordion="true" aria-controls="ot-desc-id-C0002" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0002"></button><!-- Accordion header --><div class="ot-acc-hdr"><div class="ot-plus-minus"><span></span><span></span></div><h4 class="ot-cat-header" id="ot-header-id-C0002">Analytical cookies</h4><div class="ot-tgl"><input type="checkbox" name="ot-group-id-C0002" id="ot-group-id-C0002" role="switch" class="category-switch-handler" data-optanongroupid="C0002" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0002"> <label class="ot-switch" for="ot-group-id-C0002"><span class="ot-switch-nob"></span> <span class="ot-label-txt">Analytical cookies</span></label> </div></div><!-- accordion detail --><div class="ot-acc-grpcntr ot-acc-txt"><p class="ot-acc-grpdesc ot-category-desc" id="ot-desc-id-C0002">These cookies allow us to count visits and traffic sources so we can measure and improve the performance of our site. They help us to know which pages are the most and least popular and see how visitors move around the site. All information these cookies collect is aggregated and therefore anonymous. If you do not allow these cookies we will not know when you have visited our site, and will not be able to monitor its performance.</p></div></div><div class="ot-accordion-layout ot-cat-item ot-vs-config" data-optanongroupid="C0003"><button aria-expanded="false" ot-accordion="true" aria-controls="ot-desc-id-C0003" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0003"></button><!-- Accordion header --><div class="ot-acc-hdr"><div class="ot-plus-minus"><span></span><span></span></div><h4 class="ot-cat-header" id="ot-header-id-C0003">Functional cookies</h4><div class="ot-tgl"><input type="checkbox" name="ot-group-id-C0003" id="ot-group-id-C0003" role="switch" class="category-switch-handler" data-optanongroupid="C0003" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0003"> <label class="ot-switch" for="ot-group-id-C0003"><span class="ot-switch-nob"></span> <span class="ot-label-txt">Functional cookies</span></label> </div></div><!-- accordion detail --><div class="ot-acc-grpcntr ot-acc-txt"><p class="ot-acc-grpdesc ot-category-desc" id="ot-desc-id-C0003">These cookies enable the website to provide enhanced functionality and personalisation. They may be set by us or by third party providers whose services we have added to our pages. If you do not allow these cookies then some or all of these services may not function properly.</p></div></div><div class="ot-accordion-layout ot-cat-item ot-vs-config" data-optanongroupid="C0004"><button aria-expanded="false" ot-accordion="true" aria-controls="ot-desc-id-C0004" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0004"></button><!-- Accordion header --><div class="ot-acc-hdr"><div class="ot-plus-minus"><span></span><span></span></div><h4 class="ot-cat-header" id="ot-header-id-C0004">Targeting cookies</h4><div class="ot-tgl"><input type="checkbox" name="ot-group-id-C0004" id="ot-group-id-C0004" role="switch" class="category-switch-handler" data-optanongroupid="C0004" aria-labelledby="ot-header-id-C0004"> <label class="ot-switch" for="ot-group-id-C0004"><span class="ot-switch-nob"></span> <span class="ot-label-txt">Targeting cookies</span></label> </div></div><!-- accordion detail --><div class="ot-acc-grpcntr ot-acc-txt"><p class="ot-acc-grpdesc ot-category-desc" id="ot-desc-id-C0004">These cookies may be set through our site by our advertising partners. They may be used by those companies to build a profile of your interests and show you relevant adverts on other sites. They do not store directly personal information, but are based on uniquely identifying your browser and internet device. If you do not allow these cookies, you will experience less targeted advertising.</p></div></div><div class="ot-accordion-layout ot-cat-item ot-vs-config" data-optanongroupid="BG58"><button
